RATING: 6
[GAMEID=9217] was a game that had quite a few recommendations as a light-medium weight game, so we decided to give it a try.  The artwork was bright and colorful and evocative of the Russian time period.  And the paper money brought back memories of [GAMEID=1406].

However, the game just didn't click with us.  Despite having a lot of different cards, most were just variations on cost and income, and the game boiled down to a very straightforward economic engine game---buy green income cards until at some point you switch over to buy blue or orange victory point cards.  The key decision is when to make that crossover, but it just wasn't a very [i]fun[/i] decision for us.  It felt very mechanical.  One of the problems was that there really wasn't a difference between the cards.  Sure, some had different incomes and costs, but in the end there were no "special abilities" to keep us interested (with just a few cards like the [i]Observatory[/i] being an exception).  As a result, every game [i]felt[/i] the same, going down the same path (income then aristocrats) even if the cards were different.  It was a very dry, mathematical numbers game.

Still, I do like the [url=http://www.westpark-gamers.de/download/sp_pc_e.php]Westpark Gamer's computer version[/url] and have played that a lot.  It really distills the game down to just a few clicks (no need for shuffling, moving cards around the board, etc.), and makes for a decent computer solitaire game that you can play almost on auto-pilot to kill some time.

RATING: 7
Very nearly Ra's equal as a light (for my tastes) strategy game.  Rated half a point lower only because the luck is less manageable than in Ra, and the early gameplay is constrained by the need to ramp up your income.  Once you have a solid income established, however, there is a pleasant variety of strategies available to choose from, and tactical play is also quite rich for a game of its weight class.  Quite an addictive game, although it may be possible to burn out on it eventually.  Suitable as a gateway game, although it may be better as a 'next' game - the game you introduce to people as their second German-style strategy game after they have been introduced to them with something else.

UPDATE: I've lowered my rating by half a point because of the Mistress of Ceremonies 'bug', the (very slight) underpricing of the Observatory, and because of the constraints that the importance of endgame Aristocrat scoring place on a player's strategic choices.  I like the aesthetic of using a mathematical series (Triangular numbers) for this, but I think 'Tummelhofer' should have used one with a slower progression like the Tribonacci or Lucas series.

UPDATE: Finally got to play this FtF.  I was the administrator, and as a result got the full brunt of the fiddly bits effect of this game.  Surprisingly this didn't bother me as much as I thought it would, although banking definitely bugged me more than managing the cards in play.  This isn't so much a comment about SP being less fiddly in this respect than I expected, it certainly is extremely fiddly in terms of flying bits.  Instead it seems my tolerance for such things is higher than I thought it would be.  So my rating won't take a hit from it, but next game I am banker OR administrator, not both.

UPDATE: I've burned out on Saint Pete a bit, and rarely play it on BSW anymore, since I want to maintain some enthusiasm for playing it with my friends FtF, since they really enjoy it.  I've dropped my rating to 7.

UPDATE: Very much looking forward to buying the expansion, which should help straighten out most of the kinks in the base game. If it does what it promises, the expansion should rate an 8+

RATING: 6
It's an engine-building euro where the stuff that builds the engine is really obtuse.
"All these green guys give me $3. Why do they cost different amounts?"
"Well, because of those icons. They might matter late in the game."
"What are the icons worth, then?"
"Well, if a particular upgrade shows up, you might be able to buy and swap it with a matching icon. If it shows up."
That sort of theme continues throughout the game, and it's unfortunately a far more coherent theme than the one the game wants to present.

RATING: 7
A classic economic Euro game were you acquire Green cards that provide you with income.  Blue building cards that score victory points.  Orange noble cards that provide income and victory points at the end of the game.  It also include bonus cards which can be any of the other card types and usually upgrades the cards.  Plays very quickly even with 4 players and should not last more than an hour.  A good "next step" game as it is very light.  

You did need the expansion though as a few cards in the base game need to be replaced as they are overpowered.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.6
Saint Petersburg 聖彼得堡 
公元十一世紀，基輔衰落，並分裂成幾個獨立公國。蒙古於公元1238年入侵，焚燒莫斯科，破壞基輔。羅斯人被蒙古人建立的金帳汗國所統治。公元1380年莫斯科公國擊敗金帳汗國，擺離昔日臣屬關係，隱然成為各公國的首領。公元1462年伊凡三世Ivan III(伊凡大帝)登上莫斯科公國王公之位，致力開疆拓土，並自稱全羅斯大公，至此俄羅斯帝國略見雛形。 
公元1672年5月30日，彼得一世Peter I(彼得大帝)誕生。彼得執掌國家大權後即厲行改革，創建正規陸軍及艦隊。其後俄羅斯在長達21年的北方戰爭中，擊敗當時的北方強國瑞典，奪得了波羅的海的出海口及東南沿岸。在彼得大帝的領導下，俄羅斯由內陸國變成瀕海國，其後更成為歐洲軍事強國，奠下俄羅斯帝國的基礎。 
公元1703年，彼得大帝在奪自瑞典的土地上興建新城。這座以彼得大帝的守護天使聖徒彼得為名的城市，即聖彼得堡Saint Petersburg。聖彼得堡位於涅瓦河Neva與芬蘭灣Gulf of Finland 交會的河口，正如聖彼得執掌天國之匙，聖彼得堡成為了俄羅斯通往大海、面向歐洲的門戶。 
公元1712年初，彼得大帝正式遷都聖彼得堡，自此一直到公元1918年的二百多年，聖彼得堡一直是俄羅斯的首都。第一次世界大戰爆發後，俄羅斯在公元1914年去掉了首都名稱中的日耳曼語系色彩，將聖彼得堡更名為彼得格勒Petergrad。公元1917年在彼得格勒發生的二月革命和十月革命，推翻了長達304年的羅曼諾夫王朝。彼得格勒因太過接近邊界，為了更能背靠俄羅斯的工農業地區，蘇俄乃決定遷都回莫斯科。 
公元1924年1月，列寧Lenin逝世後，彼得格勒更名為列寧格勒Leningrad。及至公元1991年12月蘇聯解體後，這座城市才恢復了它的原名聖彼得堡。 

遊戲目標： 
玩家以手上有限的金錢購入咭牌。透過掌控不同的咭牌，玩家必須平衡金錢和分數上的收益。在不斷增加收入的同時，玩家們必須在分數上進行競爭。遊戲完結時分數最多的玩家獲勝。 

遊戲配件： 
盧布紙鈔ruble 382張(1、2盧布各14張， 5、10盧布各12張，20盧布8張) 
勞工牌worker card 31張(面底皆以綠色為底色。牌底印有椅子圖案) 
建築牌building card 28張(面底皆以藍色為底色。牌底印有俄羅斯屋頂圖案) 
官吏牌aristocrat card 27張(面底皆以橙色為底色。牌底印有人頭側影圖案) 
替換牌trading card 30張(牌底印有綠、藍、橙三色。牌面分別是綠色、藍色及橙色為底色，各10張。牌底印有正方形圖案) 
起始玩家牌starting player card 4張(牌面分別印有椅子、正方形、人頭側影及俄羅斯屋頂圖案) 
起始玩家標記starting player marker 4個(漆上金色木製標記。分別是椅子、正方形、人頭側影及俄羅斯屋頂圖案) 
木製棋子8隻(紅、藍、黃、綠各2) 
遊戲圖板Game board 1塊(外圍印有計分表；上部為放置棄牌、勞工牌、建築牌、官吏牌及交易牌的牌疊位置；棄牌區下方是獎分表；下部分有兩行，各8個用作放置咭牌的置牌區) 

開局： 
將遊戲圖板展開放於桌上。 
將勞工牌、建築牌、官吏牌及替換牌分開。分別覆轉洗混後放到遊戲圖板適當的位置上。 
每位玩家獲發面值25盧布的紙鈔後，請將紙鈔收好。遊戲中玩家無需公開自己手持的金錢數目。 
剩下的紙鈔依面值分類，放到遊戲圖板旁作庫房bank備用。 
每位玩家獲發2隻同色的棋子。玩家需將其中1隻放到遊戲圖板左上角0分的位置上。另1隻則放在玩家面前的桌上，以標記該玩家的代表顏色。 
將起始玩家牌覆轉洗混，平均分發予每位玩家相同數目的起始玩家牌。 
若玩家數目只有3人，多出的1張起始玩家牌屬最年少的玩家所有。 
依據各玩家得到的起始玩家牌，玩家各自拿取配對的起始玩家標記。 
將所有起始玩家牌放回盒中棄用。 
由最年長的玩家主持遊戲。他將負責抽牌、點算金錢，及為每位玩家計算分數。 
依據玩家數目，遊戲主持拿起勞工牌疊，從頂翻開8張勞工牌(4人遊戲)，從左到右逐一放到遊戲圖板的上行咭牌位置。3人遊戲翻開6張；2人遊戲翻開4張。 
遊戲主持放回牌疊時，需將牌疊直放，以標示遊戲每回合的進度。一般情況下牌疊皆為橫放。 

遊玩： 
這遊戲以回合進行。每回合包含4個階段。完成4個階段後，回合結束。遊戲將從新開始另一回合。直至遊戲結束。 

每回合的流程： 
勞工階段；起始玩家標記是椅子圖案。 
建築階段；起始玩家標記是俄羅斯屋頂圖案。 
官吏階段；起始玩家標記是人頭側影圖案。 
替換階段；起始玩家標記是正方形圖案。 
若遊戲尚未結束，各玩家將持有的起始玩家標記交予其左方的玩家。 

勞工階段、建築階段及官吏階段，每個階段皆以下列步驟組成： 
1. 玩家行動 
2. 收取回報 
3. 補充咭牌 
替換階段則沒有收取回報這個步驟。因此遊戲圖板替換牌牌疊的位置上，並沒有印上金錢和分數圖案。 

1. 玩家行動 
由持有這階段之起始玩家標記的玩家開始，依順時針次序，每位玩家輪流執行1個行動。 
放棄執行行動的玩家，在稍後再輪至他時，仍可重新選擇是否執行行動。 
例：玩家依順時針方向的次序為甲、乙、丙、丁。玩家甲、乙依次序完成一項行動後，丙棄權。丁完成行動後，甲、乙棄權。丙現在可重新考慮是否執行行動。 
一旦所有玩家都連續放棄執行行動，玩家行動步驟立即完結。這條件與誰是起始玩家無關。 
例：最後執行行動的玩家是乙。玩家丙、丁及甲棄權。一旦乙選棄權，則行動步驟結束。 
當輪至玩家執行行動時，玩家可選執行以下4項的其中之一： 
買牌buy：將遊戲圖板上翻開的咭牌，放到玩家的桌前。 
取牌add：將遊戲圖板上翻開的咭牌，放到玩家的手牌之中。 
打牌play：將手牌中的咭牌，放到玩家的桌前。 
棄權pass：放棄執行行動。 

買牌 
玩家從遊戲圖板上，放在置牌區內的咭牌中，選出1張咭牌(任何種類皆可)放到自己的桌前。 
計算該咭牌的價格後，玩家需即時支付金錢予庫房。 
放到玩家桌前的咭牌，即可以在往後的收取回報步驟中，為玩家帶來回報。 

取牌 
玩家從遊戲圖板上，放在置牌區內的咭牌中，選出1張咭牌(任何種類皆可)加到自己的手牌中。 
玩家的手牌最多只可有3張咭牌。手牌中的咭牌並無任何效用。 

打牌 
玩家從手牌中，選出1張咭牌(任何種類皆可)放到自己的桌前。 
計算該咭牌的價格後，玩家需即時支付金錢予庫房。 
放到玩家桌前的咭牌，即可以在往後的收取回報步驟中，為玩家帶來回報。 

棄權 
玩家放棄執行任何行動。 
若玩家行動步驟尚未完結，則輪至其左方玩家執行行動。 

2. 收取回報 
檢視各玩家的桌前，根據各人擁有的咭牌，分別計算各人的回報。 
玩家桌前的咭牌先依牌面顏色分成3類，會較方便計算回報。 
不同階段中，各玩家依不同種類的咭牌，計算這些咭牌中錢幣及盾牌印明之數字的總和。玩家可以收到等同該數字的金錢及分數。 
一般來說勞工牌會為玩家帶來金錢；建築牌則為玩家帶來分數；官吏牌及替換牌則可能為玩家帶來金錢及分數。 

回報： 
勞工階段中，各玩家點算自己桌前牌面是綠色底色的咭牌(即勞工牌或替換牌)。依綠色咭牌中錢幣及盾牌印明的數字，玩家可以收到該數字的金錢及分數。 
建築階段中，各玩家點算自己桌前牌面是藍色底色的咭牌(即建築牌或替換牌)。依藍色咭牌中錢幣及盾牌印明的數字，玩家可以收到該數字的金錢及分數。 
官吏階段中，各玩家點算自己桌前牌面是橙色底色的咭牌(即官吏牌或替換牌)。依橙色咭牌中錢幣及盾牌印明的數字，玩家可以收到該數字的金錢及分數。 
替換階段並不包含收取回報這步驟。 

3. 補充咭牌 
遊戲圖板下部分有兩行，分別8個用作放置咭牌的位置，構成2行8列的置牌區。 
每列置牌區都只可放置1張咭牌，即遊戲圖板上最多只可放有8張咭牌。 
遊戲主持將遊戲圖板上，先將下行置牌區的咭牌全數靠右排列。這步驟在第一回合並不會出現。替換階段中無需理會此項。 
遊戲主持將遊戲圖板上，先將上行置牌區的咭牌盡量靠右排列。因為每列置牌區都只可放置1張咭牌，若下行置牌區放有咭牌，則上行的咭牌只好排在最右的空列。 
依直放牌疊的種類，遊戲主持拿起下一個橫放牌疊，翻開足夠的咭牌。將咭牌放到置牌區，讓遊戲圖板上補足8張咭牌。 
例：下行置牌區只剩1張咭牌，上行則剩2張咭牌。遊戲主持先將下行的1張咭牌放到下行最右一列。上行的2張咭牌則只可移至上行最右的第二及第三列。遊戲主持需翻開5張咭牌，放到上行最在的5列中。 
若遊戲圖板上經已有8張咭牌，則遊戲主持無需翻開新的咭牌。 
若牌疊沒有足夠的咭牌，在遊戲圖板上少於8張咭牌的情況下繼續遊戲。 
早前直放牌疊恢復橫放，遊戲主持放下牌疊時則需直放，以表示遊戲進入另一階段。 
勞工階段時，遊戲主持需以建築牌補足8張咭牌；建築階段時，遊戲主持需以官吏牌補足8張咭牌；官吏階段時，遊戲主持需以替換牌補足8張咭牌。 
替換階段時，下行置牌區的咭牌全數棄用，變作棄牌。原先在上行置牌區的咭牌，則全數移到下行。遊戲主持需以勞工牌補足8張咭牌。 

咭牌的價格： 
每張咭牌的左上角皆印有一個數字。該數字即是這咭牌的基本價格。 
買牌或打牌時，依據玩家桌前的咭牌，玩家每擁有一張同樣的咭牌，則可獲減1盧布的折扣。 
買牌時，若該咭牌是放在下行置牌區的咭牌，則可獲減1盧布的折扣。 
買牌或打牌時，若玩家桌前放有木工場Carpenter workshop，而該咭牌的牌面是藍色底色的話，則可獲減1盧布的折扣。 
買牌或打牌時，若玩家桌前放有煉金場Gold smelter，而該咭牌的牌面是橙色底色的話，則可獲減1盧布的折扣。 
以上折扣皆可累積。只要條件合適，這些折扣同時有效。 
縱使折扣大於咭牌的基本價格，所有咭牌的最低價格仍是1盧布。 
例：玩家甲決定買下放在下行置牌區中的伐木工Lumberjack。玩家甲檢視放在自己桌前的咭牌，他經已擁有2張伐木工，故此他可獲合共3盧布的折扣。伐木工的基本價格是3盧布，所以玩家甲仍要支付1盧布。。 

替換牌的使用： 
若玩家是以替換牌作買牌或打牌時，玩家必須在自己桌前的咭牌中，棄掉另1張咭牌。 
遭棄掉的咭牌，必須與剛打出的替換牌種類相同(即牌面的底色相同)。即以藍色的換掉藍色的建築牌，橙色的換掉橙色的官吏牌。 
使用綠色的替換牌則多了一項限制。每張綠色咭牌的右上方有一個圖案(木板、毛皮、船隻、布匹及金塊)，被換掉的勞工牌必需印有與替換牌相同的圖案。 
玩家不可棄掉替換牌，以換上另一張替換牌。 

替換牌的價值： 
每張替換牌的左上角皆印有其基本價格。 
只要條件合適，一般咭牌之折扣同樣適用於替換牌。 
將替換牌加上折扣後的價格，與被換掉的咭牌之基本價格比較。若替換牌的價格較高時，玩家需支付其差額予庫房。 
縱使兩者差額等於或少於0，玩家最少仍要支付1盧布。 

終局： 
當補充咭牌時，若某牌疊的所有咭牌皆已耗用(即放置牌疊的位置上完全沒有咭牌)，則這回合即成為最後一個回合。這回合結束後遊戲立時完結。 

勝負： 
計算各玩家桌前之橙色咭牌的種類數目，擁有越多不同的官吏，玩家獎分越多。 
第一種官職1分；第二種官職2分；第三種官職3分；第四種官職4分；如此類推。這項獎分只累進至10種官職，多於10種的官職將不會增加分數。 
例：依獎分表，擁有11名官吏合共10種官職可讓玩家多得55分(1+2+3……+10)。 
計算各玩家擁有的金錢，每10盧布可得1分。 
檢查各玩家的手牌數目。每擁有1張咭牌，玩家將被扣去5分。 
擁有分數最多的玩家獲勝。 
分數相同則以金錢多寡分勝負。金錢多者獲勝。 

勞工牌： 
勞工牌的面底皆以綠色為底色，牌底印有椅子圖案。 
勞工牌只為玩家帶來金錢收入。 

伐木工Lumberjack 6張(基本價格3) 
伐木工可被替換為木工場Carpenter workshop。 

採金工Gold miner 6張(基本價格4) 
採金工可被替換為煉金場Gold smelter。 

牧羊人Shepherd 6張(基本價格5) 
牧羊人可被替換為織造廠Weaving mill。 

毛皮販Fur trapper 6張(基本價格6) 
毛皮販可被替換為毛皮廠Fur Shop。 

造船工Ship builder 6張(基本價格7) 
造船工可被替換為造船廠Wharf。 

沙皇及木匠Czar and carpenter (基本價格8) 
沙皇彼得熱忡於木工及造船。那時的木匠們可說是自成另一階級。 
這咭牌可被任何綠色的替換牌所替換。 

建築牌： 
建築牌的面底皆以藍色為底色。牌底印有俄羅斯屋頂圖案。 
建築牌大多可為玩家帶來分數。 

市集Market 5張(基本價格5) 

關所Customs house 5張(基本價格8) 

消防署Fire house 3張(基本價格11) 

療養院Hospital 3張(基本價格14) 

圖書館Library 3張(基本價格17) 

劇院Theater 2張(基本價格20) 

學院Academy (基本價格23) 

普希金村Potjomkin’s village (基本價格2/6) 
這咭牌的基本價格是2盧布。 
在被任何藍色的替換牌所替換時，這咭牌的基本價格作6盧布計算。這即是說玩家最多可節省4盧布。 

酒館Pub 2張(基本價格1) 
在建築階段中，收取回報步驟後，玩家每支付2盧布可換取1分。 
擁有1間酒館的玩家每次最多可換取5分。擁有2間酒館的玩家每次最多可換取10分。 
玩家不可以分數換取金錢。 

倉庫Warehouse (基本價格2) 
擁有倉庫的玩家，其手牌最多可持有4張咭牌。 

天文台Observatory 2張(基本價格6) 
在建築階段中，玩家行動步驟時，玩家可從4個牌疊中的其中一個中，抽取1張咭牌。 
若牌疊中只剩下1張咭牌，玩家不可從這牌疊抽牌。這是為了避免因這特殊行動觸及終局條件。 
玩家可將新得到的咭牌，如常支付代價後放到自己的桌前；或將這咭牌加進手牌之中；或將這咭牌放到棄牌中。 
這行動每回合只可執行一次，並將取代玩家的正常行動。 
執行完上述行動後，在收取回報步驟時，玩家不可拿取天文台的1分。玩家可將咭牌橫放作識別。 

官吏牌： 
官吏牌的面底皆以橙色為底色。牌底印有人頭側影圖案。 
官吏牌可為玩家帶來金錢或分數。 

文書Author 6張(基本價格4) 

行政官Administrator 5張(基本價格7) 

司庫官Warehouse manager 5張(基本價格10) 

書記官Secretary 4張(基本價格12) 

審計官Controller 3張(基本價格14) 

審判官Judge 2張(基本價格16) 

典儀官Mistress of Ceremonies 2張(基本價格18) 

替換牌： 
替換牌的牌底印有綠、藍、橙三色。牌面則分別是綠色、藍色及橙色為底色。牌底印有正方形圖案。 
依據替換牌牌面的顏色，它必須用以交換其他牌面顏色相同的咭牌。 

木工場Carpenter workshop(基本價格4) 
支付代價後，玩家可用木工場替換伐木工、或沙皇及木匠。 
擁有木工場的玩家，在支付藍色咭牌的費用時可獲減1盧布的折扣。 

煉金場Gold smelter(基本價格6) 
支付代價後，玩家可用煉金場替換採金工、或沙皇及木匠。 
擁有煉金場的玩家，在支付橙色咭牌的費用時可獲減1盧布的折扣。 

織造廠Weaving mill 2張(基本價格8) 
支付代價後，玩家可用織造廠替換牧羊人、或沙皇及木匠。 

毛皮廠Fur Shop 3張(基本價格10) 
支付代價後，玩家可用毛皮廠替換毛皮販、或沙皇及木匠。 

造船廠Wharf 3張(基本價格12) 
支付代價後，玩家可用造船廠替換造船工、或沙皇及木匠。 

銀行Bank(基本價格13) 

凱薩琳宮Catherine the Great Palace(基本價格17) 

基督復活教堂Church of the Resurrection of Jesus Christ(基本價格16) 

港口Harbor(基本價格16) 

隱士廬Hermitage(基本價格18) 

馬林斯基劇院Mariinsky theater(基本價格10) 
在建築階段中，收取回報步驟時，馬林斯基劇院的收入等同玩家擁有的橙色咭牌數目。 

彼得夏宮Peterhof(基本價格14)

In a game of experienced players it's transformed into an optimization game, but it can take many plays before you reach that state.

RATING: 9
Wow always a great game. Always advise new players not to spend all there money at once at the start on an expensive building as they will struggle to recover. 

I have the old Czech version with the nice artwork and have no interest in picking up the new version with the additional market and expanded 5 player count. Artwork counts a lot towards my enjoyment of a game and the new version, for me, is awful. Haven't played the expansion for the original game so can't comment on that but would love to get it.

Just a great game. Probably my favourite game with paper money (can't think of a better one right now, and why did I even think of that category??).

UPDATE

I hadn't played this one for a while and this game made me think about it slightly differently. I will say this was an older Czech version of the game without the additional market and 5 player rules. 

This game has always been in my personal top ten since I first played it. I have always thought of it as a kind of gateway game as long as you explained the need to generate a money engine and not overspend at the beginning on any one card. Go for a bit of everything and then start focusing on collecting the aristocrats.

Well I had the feeling it wasn't a great experience for one of the players, and they were very eloquent as to the reasons why and it did make me think about the game. It is true that the game has absolutely no catch-up mechanism and I guess in this way it is showing its age if you are used to games giving a more even experience. It's true if you over spend or mis-manage spending you are very unlikely to catch up as there is no in-built mechanism to aid this. Also once you fall behind on the financial benefits of courting the craftsmen you are also going to be hard pressed to catch up in this respect of generating income.

The comments were spot on and I can completely see the validity of them, it just made me think about the different experiences gamers can expect in modern game design. Saint Petersburg came out in 2004, and I guess for some people now, it is showing its age ... But for me even if I had to reduce my collection to just 10 games I suspect it would still be there on my shelf, as its overall experience, game play and decision making is unique and I really enjoy it.

RATING: 9
Upgraded to a 9.  My wife and I still enjoy this one.  A fun, couple game that doesn't require too much strategy.  Timing what you are concentrating in phases of the game is important - buildings are very important to winning but only if you make sure to keep up with Nobles.  The Nobles also pay so getting them early is important instead of buildings as one strategy.  The strategy of getting an expensive building early because its points will add up over time does not seem to work - too expensive too early.  The game's artistic design is superb. 
For those who think Nobles are the true path to success, I just won the game where I had only 7 nobles and my wife had 10 (giving her a 27 point difference at the end) but it wasn't enough for her to win.  Buying cheaper buildings at the beginning and upgrading them along with point-laden Nobles can give you a tremendous point lead.  So there's another winning strategy.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
This is a brilliantly executed game. The rules are fairly simple, but the interactions are subtle and interesting. We spent our first game thinking I was hosed, then that someone else was hosed, and then wound up within 10 points of each other -- and had two of us not made bad plays in the final round, we'd have been two points apart. Unlike some games, that tightness didn't feel forced or artificial.

The rhythm of the game -- filling slots with available cards, who goes first in each round, buying vs. taking and playing, how cards get scored -- is unique, tense at times (and very enjoyably so), and leads a great mix of strategy and tactics. Its brilliance is understated in its expression, but it's there.

It's pretty too. I especially like the subtle gold details in the cards and the period feel of the artwork. I do wish the insert worked a bit better (when stored sideways, all the cards get mixed up), but that's a minor complaint. I even get why this game uses paper money, which I generally loathe: You look at your money a lot, and it needs to be secret; there's not really a better way to meet those criteria than paper money.

St. Pete is a gem.

RATING: 7
[i]Saint Petersburg[/i] is a very dry game (ooh, my favorite) that is all about being able to anticipate future income while setting your future expenses appropriately (by taking appropriately priced cards into your hand).

I have done well so far by following a strategy of being constantly almost-but-not-quite-broke.  I try to have just enough money to play a card in the current phase while taking cards into hand that I will be able to play in the next phase or two.  What cards I take depends on the payments I will receive at the end of the current/next phase.  Occasionally, I have taken duplicate orange cards just to block an opponent who is trying to steamroll the end-game set collection bonus, especially if they aren't too expensive.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Game in a Nutshell: Card-based, engine-building game of investing in making money vs. points.  

Played as: 2,3 player live; 2,3,4 player on Yucata.de

Played with: New Society Expansion (2,4 player on Yucata.de)

Pros: Smooth flowing mechanics with an un-assuming tactical heart. I specifically enjoy how different cards are scored at different times. It creates this inner struggle of what I want now vs. what's going to be good for me later; especially in the early rounds when moneys very tight. Gives you a nice shot of uncluttered euro in under an hour.  

Cons: Very straight forward strategically. Requires players of relatively equal skill to be competitive. Minimal interaction. Has a run-away leader problem where the game's outcome can probably be told with 85% accuracy after the first 2-3 rounds (especially in two-player games). Finally, I don't necessarily mind it, but it's pretty clearly a math game.

Other: It took me one game to understand that it's pretty straight-forward strategically and must gain any lasting power from subtle tactical play. Even at that, if you really dig in, I don't think the tactical decisions are that advanced after a dozen or so plays on average. For me, the game peaked somewhere between 5-10 plays. There seems to be more life in the game with three or four players while I'll likely avoid two-player gamers because of the way it seems to amplify the game's problems exponentially.

Best Use: Quick hitting, medium-light euro when you need a fix.

RATING: 9
Too long and strategic to be a super filler but quick playing, this game is a new favorite. Turns are so short you're never disengaged. Card availability variance forces varying strategies. This is the distillation of an economic engine game to its most basic parts. Players are forced to balance money and point earning power, but as (most) every card scores every round, there is no pinpointed pivot, rather a huge gray area across the widest expanse of the midgame. Easy to pick up but with lots of room for strategic growth and always a fun time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I thought I would like this game, because it was compared to San Juan, but I don't. There are a lot of no-brainer decisions on buying cards, such as until the last few rounds, you should always buy any worker card you can get your hands on, starting with the cheapest. They will all pay for themselves in 1 to 3 rounds. A silly tactic then seems to be to manipulate the number of workers that will be available, so that if you're first in the round, the number of workers mod the number of players is 1, and you get one more worker than the other players. This extends to other categories of card, though not as much.

There is marginal difference between value per cost of different cards, and not much you can do in combination to improve upon that. I've heard the trick is that every investment is profitable, but if you make every investment you won't have the cash on hand to make the best investment when it becomes available. I don't really grasp how to recognize the best investment. Maybe if I did, I'd appreciate this game more.

RATING: 5
"Better than San Juan"?  Apples and oranges, but I still disagree.  This is an excessively computational game in which there is often one move you can make which is obviously superior to all others, and every veteran player approaches the game pretty much the same way.  It also doesn't help that you're already half-way to victory if you're lucky enough to get a first-turn Judge or Mistress of Ceremonies.  I don't hate the game, but I've had my fill of it.

RATING: 6
Don't judge this one by your first impression - multiple plays were needed before I appreciated this game. My first game was a disaster - I had no idea what I was trying to do until more than halfway through the game (it didn't help that I was taught the game by a native German speaker that couldn't convey much subtlety in English, so I was given the how-to but none of the why). Subsequent playings revealed some very interesting strategies, though I do question if one (collecting aristocrats) is maybe too powerful. I look forward to exploring this game some more and seeing if my concerns are valid or if the game has even more layers waiting to be discovered. ***UPDATE 8/13/04*** After many more plays, I am convinced that you must focus on the aristocrat race. Assuming all players understand this, the game then devolves into a pretty banal race to see who gets the best cards on their turn. You can try and convince me otherwise (especially those delusional souls that compare this game to Puerto Rico - blasphemy!) but I have played enough of this game in particluar and of these games in general to know what I'm talking about.***UPDATE 5/14/05*** After more than a hundred computer games and half-a-dozen more face-to-face meetings, I feel I have to bump the rating to a 6... regardless of the game's limitations, I still enjoy playing it, and that's the bottom line, right?

RATING: 7
Sankt Petersburg is a perfect example of a German-styled engine game, and has got a quite clear mechanic that can be explained easily: starting with a limited sum of money, players have got to buy and display cards on their boards that bring them money and points. This proceeds in four phases with separate scorings.

Even though the outcome of the game can be decided by luck in quite a harsh way, Sankt Petersburg offers variety from one play to another as money and points are seldom available at the same time (if at all). Plus, managing resources is especially tricky - more often than not players have got to walk on a thin rope not to become bankrupt.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
St. Petersburg is one of my favorite games to play.  It is essentially a card game with money and a game board used for displaying the cards and the scoring track.  At its core, it's an engine building game (money, points).  Throughout the game players must decide how to invest their money.  Workers do not produce any points but do provide income;  buildings provide points but no income; nobles provide money and/or points but at a lower rate than workers and builders.  Nobles however have an end-game scoring bonus.  The winning player is often the one who best times the shift from money to points.  Additionally players may take up to three cards and keep them 'in hand'.  They must pay for them by game end or lose points.  While simple, balancing this mechanic is essential for winning the game.  This game sees a lot of plays in my game group.  I consider it a classic for its elegant design and high replay value.

RATING: 9
El Zar busca modernizar su imperio reubicando su capital en la ciudad de San Petersburgo. Esto genera un masivo traslado de la Corte a la ciudad y la necesidad de construir todas las comodidades necesarias para acomodarlos. En San Petersburgo los jugadores representarán a nobles prominentes que contratarán trabajadores y construirán edificios para obtener Rublos y atraer aristócratas para aumentar su prestigio.

San Petersburgo es un juego muy fácil de aprender. En cada fase del turno habrá 8 cartas que los jugadores podrán comprar y esto se repetirá cuatro veces en cada turno (para trabajadores, edificios, aristócratas y comercio). Esa genial simplicidad lo hace muy accesible a todo tipo de jugadores.

El encanto de San Petersburgo es que es adictivo. Con una dinámica muy fluida, el juego terminará en una media hora y siempre dejará las ganas de volver a jugar, para probar nuevas estrategias y combinaciones de cartas. La estética está muy bien adaptada a la temática y se pueden reconocer entre las cartas algunos edificios emblemáticos de la ciudad.

PS: Basic "Through the Ages". Buy this one before you go for TTA
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Excellent game that's mid-weight and easy to relearn and teach. A great game for week nights and perfect for 2-players. In this game you have 4 stacks of cards (workers, buildings, aristocrats and upgrade cards). The first phase of the game you may purchase workers or any remaining cards on the board from previous rounds. At the end of the phase you will be paid the coin amounts on the cards displayed in front of you. Next phase you can purchase buildings and at the end of the phase you will score victory points. The 3rd phase you may purchase aristocrats, which will also bring money and possibly victory points. And the last phase you can purchase upgrades to your currently purchased cards.

It's all very simple, the cards are displayed each phase for you to peruse and decide what works best for your strategy. There are 3 things you can do on a turn: 1. Purchase a card and display it in front of you, 2. Take a card into your hand and buy it later and 3. Pass

Set collection works so well in that it allows for cheaper costs on like items and provides a great way to upgrade these cheap cards later. 

Wonderful game that we have had for some time and gets few plays, but when it comes out we enjoy it greatly.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I'm glad I didn't read this site before we bought this game for my brother-in-law for Christmas.  We loved the game!  After 2-3 games, we all thought we had mastered the common Aristocrat strategy that so many complain of.  But we found that tweaking that strategy for nuances was really fun.  My wife just won with a building strategy I thought was premature, but she stayed close enough in the Aristocrat race to leverage her game-long building point advantage.

I love the balancing act of buildings vs. everything else, the balancing of your hand, keeping track of future slots, risk taking--whether you can leave something to the next turn or go for it on the bottom row, the timing of purchases from your hand, prioritizing different types of upgrades, and the occasional successful denial of a crucial Aristocrat, etc.  Comebacks are difficult, but very fulfilling when accomplished.  

And unlike most, I LOVE the look of this game.  I love the funky character drawings, the neat historical buildings, the slightly-off-the-normal colors of the cards, and the look of the money.  I like the symbols on the cards, the neat, golden wood versions of the symbols, and the colorful, but muted board.  Take a minute to look at the background details of the board--it's quite nice.   

One small negative--the money is little and slick and kind of hard to use.  We also dislike the game with 2 players.  It's too tit-for-tat and boring.  It's already a game of small dollar by dollar differences--it needs that little bit of unpredictable human factor and worrying about 3 or 4 slots available for cards to make 
it fun.  
The game also occupies a unique niche because I have not played anything similar.  As I said, there a few similarities to other games in terms of being efficient from a common set of options, but the duplication and row mechanisms and tiny dollar by dollar savings to manipulate are unique.  Not everyone will like this, but you should try it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Nice game, with fairly straightforward rules, and the few "special ability" cards are quite simple. 

This is a game of rhythms and patterns. To become proficient, I think you not only need to play several games, but within a small enough time period that you can apply what you have learned and build your skills.

Money management is definitely one key, which includes choosing the right cards at the right times. If you are just a couple rubles short now and then, it can really hurt you. Knowing who choses first in the next phase is also important. Plus there are a few cards that are especially strong (but not overpowered).

It's not aggressive, but there are some subtle interactions beyond just taking a card someone else needs (which only rarely hurts them more than you). Notably taking more or fewer cards from the pool causes fewer or more cards to get drawn in the next phase, which can have quite an effect.

The "rules" weight is probably a 2, while the "strategy" weight is probably a 3.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
A city-building card game that reminds me of San Juan in feel, although the mechanics are more complex.  San Juan is a hand management game, Saint Petersburg is a card drafting game.  Although I said it is more complex than San Juan, it doesn't feel heavy, or draggy.  Saint Petersburg is just a nice medium weight euro.

Although it is over-boxed, it has high quality bits: gilded highlights on linen finish cards, golden wooden tokens, and a board that does not have much purpose, but does organize the game in a helpful manner, and track victory points.

[update]Saint Petersburg has a particularly nasty zero-sum "economic snowball".  That means, if you are playing someone who knows what they are doing, and you make one wrong move early in the game, you are likely to lose by 40 points or so. Your opponent could easily double your score.  It is a very brutal game.  I have dropped my rating by a point and I'm not sure if I want to keep it.  

Also, the aristocrats are overpowered, and the buildings are underpowered. That bugs me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Very nice, although the game is a bit repetitive and the strategy does not give many possible choices, but to buy many workers as fast as possible at the beginning. The problem is the total absence of interaction, but to buy useless cards to take them away from your opponent. At the end of the game, you feel like having spent some time alone, and meet your friends that just arrived. Works really well with 2 players, of course maintaining the total lack of interaction. A good point is that the strategy changes a lot depending from the number of players: with more players money is less and palaces importance changes. The rule about which you don't get more points by having more than 10 nobles is good when in two players, because you need to buy otherwise useless palaces, but even reduces interaction making even less useful to buy nobles and exchange cards to contrast the opponent. In a 2 player game the exchange cards IMHO are almost always completely useless, unless they have special capabilities, in which case they are even too powerful. Not very well balanced after all.

RATING: 7
Simple buy-cards-and-have-victory-points game, but it has some deeper value. Of course it's heavily luck based that which cards are shown and which your opponents buy.
Also cunning systems are the expansions (if you buy any, you'll just probably be left without any money to buy proper basic green cards).
Another cunning one is the changing starting player on every round. Set taking aspect is in the orange cards, which also give you bonuses if you have many different kinds of them at the game's end.
It feels as if there are various tactics and ways to win, definitely a game which gives you something to explore for a long time.

Didn't make the cut- I don't keep broken games.

*Update
Yep. Watching Tom/Melody Vasel's playthrough, I discovered that the problem was that I was not flushing the lower row of cards at the end of the round. As a result, things stacked up and the momentum of the game stalled.

RATING: 8
-
Update:  05/18/06
Rating increased from 7.5 to 8.
Great game, but the reasons I'm not rating it higher are the slight luck of the draw (Observatory and Mistress of Ceremonies) and the player positional right/left binding (sitting to the left of a less experienced player is a big advantage).

I will leave my original comments (below) for the record, but I have to admit most of it about the "flaw" and the value of the Observatory card were overblown. After many more plays I've concluded that this is a great game as is.

In 2- and 3-player games you don't even need the Observatory and if you concentrate too much effort on the Aristocrats, you will lose miserably. In 4-player games the Observatory and the Aristocrats become somewhat more important, but even then not to the point of guaranteeing you the game.

--------------------------------------

Original comments from 2005:

This is a fantastic game full of tough decision making and resource management. I would have rated it 8.5 (instead of 7.5) if it weren't for a major flaw (for which I'm proposing my easy fix).

The flaw is the "Observatory" card.  It is extremely powerful, and when the game is played among reasonably good players, the one who buys this card and gets to use it first, will almost always win. The 'Aristocrat' (orange) cards are key to winning this game, and the Observatory is key to winning the Aristocrat cards.

The fix to this flaw is fortunately only a simple minor rule change. This change would virtually eliminate the huge imbalancing effect of this card.

The normal rule is that the owner of the Obsevatory may pick up the top card from any of the four stacks and either buy it, reserve it for future purchase, or discard it, and 99% of the time the selected card is an Aristocrat one. My proposed change is to limit the options of the Observatoy holder to just purchasing the drawn card out right. If he doesn't have the money or chooses not to buy it, he may not discard it or reserve it to be purchased later.  Instead, the next player will have the option to buy it. If the second player also chooses not to buy it, then the third player will have the option to buy, and so on. If no one buys it, then it will go to the discard pile. In my opinion, this simple rule change will improve the game balance tremendously.  Yet, a less atractive alternative would be to simply remove the two Observatory cards from the game.  

-

RATING: 9
[floatleft][ImageID=258831][/floatleft][b][u]Initial Impressions:[/u][/b]
Saint Petersburg is a card game disguised as a board game.

[b][u]What I like:[/u][/b]
I really enjoy playing Saint Petersburg. At its essence this game is simply an economic engine building game. Its fun to watch your engine steadily grow. 

[b][u]What I dislike:[/u][/b]
My only real gripe with St. Pete is that it can be very easy to fall behind and not be able to catch back up. 

[b][u]Overall:[/u][/b]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
A tight, tense card/machine building game.  The art is bright and atmospheric; reminiscent of Eastern European icon paintings. The gameplay is clever and full of tough decisions every time. Can be a little challenging to teach, but once everyone gets the hang of it, the game is fast and tactical fun. There's some luck of the draw, but it helps to keep the game fresh, rather than turning it into a fortune-fest 
A couple of complaints: the tiny cards are a bit flimsy, and I despise paper money.  So, the component quality is tolerable (and probably necessary), but I like what I like.

RATING: 7.25
This was a very simple and enteraining game.  There are four phases to a turn.  You score on the first three phases, while the fourth allows you to upgrade.  The first phase there is a round where everyone can buy laborer(s).  At the end you earn money (likely) and points (unlikely).  The second phase you purchase buildings.  At the end you earn money (unlikely) and points (likely).  The third phase you can buy a specialist.  At the end you earn money (unlikely) and points (likely).  During the fourth phase you can upgrade any of the three previous round cards.

It's a pretty cool game.

RATING: 7
Have played many times now.  This game has grown on me, I've changed my rating from a 5 to a 7.
GOOD BITS:
-- Many subtle decisions.
-- Plays quite quick and makes a good two player game.

BAD BITS:
-- Some basic cards broken.  I've hand drawn the errata in my set.
-- Rich get richer game.  Sometimes a player falls hopelessly behind.

HOUSE RULE:
-- In two player game on first turn the first player can buy most expensive and least expensive peasant, or the middle two, their choice.  This helps prevent one player from getting a big head start early.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Rather quick playing Euro-style card game. In the beginning you mainly invest in your money-engine (green cards) and switch later to victory point generation by  buying either buildings (continuous VP generation) or nobles (massive scoring at the end). The game rewards collecting sets of the same building (decreased price). This also contributes to the level of randomness, which I  think to be quite high (you can get a very good start if you either get cheaper crafstmen or a set of your craftsmen with fitting upgrades). 

The art-work is not very appealing, but the design is still very functional and fits to the game's quick playing nature. The down-side of this is that St. Petersburg feels very mechanical. Additionally there is not a lot of interaction between the players.

Hans im Glück
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
22-02-2015. Rated after 1 play. We played a basegame with some expansions thrown in. Saint Petersburg is a fun engine-building game.

Each turn, resolves around going through 4 phases (green for workers, blue for buildings, orange for nobles and multicolored stuff). Each phase begins with drawing up cards so that there are 8 cards available for purchase. All players then take turns buying and building cards and drawing cards into the hand (up to 3), or pass. If you build a card, some need to replace other cards AND you can build over another building for a discount of the cost of the previous building. After all players have consecutively passed, the phase ends. After the end of each phase, you score the VPs and get income for the cards in the color of the phase you have built.

Saint Petersburg is a fun game, but prone to an explosion of AP because you get more and more cards/abililties/ stuff to look at. I think the game is best with 2 or 3 likely, and as I played with 5 I felt downtime was a little heavy.

RATING: 6
Perhaps the geekiest game ever.  Hardly any fun at all, but compelling and interesting to play.  My only complaint about it is that there are limited winning strategies.  It's pretty much: a.) grab as many workers as you can get early; b.) grab the aristocrats to produce the second tier of income; then c.) make up for lost time on the buildings.  It's not that simple of course, but it's not that far from the mark either.  Beautiful art on the board and the cards.  Doing the math and paying out the money is a drag.  All in all, I like the game, but I can see playing it less and less every year.

RATING: 7
St. Petersburg -- Played three- and four-player.  Upon my first play, I thought there was something inelegant about the game-flow, and the play itself had a mechanical quality.  That said, I had a really good time playing it, once I knew how the moves go.

RATING: 3
A deeply flawed game with some nifty mechanics which don't really coalesce into any sort of balance. It is reasonably fun to play, but after a few games the problems begin to surface.

It is easy to fall behind at the beginning and stay behind the whole game. There is really nothing you can do to catch up.

The random nature of not only what flips up, but how many, means that players almost always win just by being in the right seat at the right time.

The Observatory is broken if it shows up in the first round of the game.

And the aristocrat bonus makes the building points practically useless. I tried having the buildings give an additional bonus points at the end of the game, but it wasn't enough.

Suggest:

2 pts/aristocrat at the end of the game, period.

Eliminate the Observatory or make it a "use once and discard" building.

Auction off turn order each phase, or try something like Power Grid auctions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Played once with 4P. A rather dry and calculative game, with the calculation bit providing room for downtime in the game. Games against the AI can be finished in mere minutes, in comparison to the only face-to-face game I played which took 1.5 hours. 

I like how cards are which are not sold off gradually clog the display and are sold off with a small discount the next round if you wait. The ability to hold on to cards seems quite simple, but also provides some of the more challenging decisions in the game. Apart from those plus points, this is an economic engine-building game where most of the parts aren't too exciting. Knowing the deck definitely helps, although buying nobles seems to be the default strategy as their endgame bonus is huge. I'm not really inspired by the dry maths involved, but this isn't a bad game either.

RATING: 7
I played this for the first time tonight, placing 2nd in a 4 player game. The mechanics are pretty simple. It's a resource game. You buy resources and they produce either cash to buy more resources or victory points. I like the mechanic of the variable turn order and order within the turn, although I don't think we completely followed that during this game. I was leading right up until the last turn, when I realized that the more different kinds of aristocrats you had in play, the more VP's you earned at the end of game scoring. So, while I scored for having 4 different aristocrats for 10 VP's, my closest competitor scored for having 9 arist's for 45 points. He won by 12 points. Only one of the four players had played before, so it was a situation where played based on his knowledge of the rules without refering to the rule book. That lead me to believe that I would lose the number of VP's equal to the cost of whatever cards I had in my hand at the end of the game, rather than the actual rule of losing 5 VP's per card. Also, I don't think we were moving the cards from the top to bottom and then off the board correctly. But, overall I enjoyed the game. I think it's a game that my daughter and boyfriend will play. I also think my regular gaming group might like to give it a shot. There's no dice, so that's always a plus with me. ;) I know where to get this game at a good price, so I'll probably buy it.

RATING: 3
I can't say that this is a bad game.  But, while I feel that the game is sound, I don't feel like I'm doing anything significant.  Most of the time this is just accounting.  

Who am I here?  

I have a couple serious gripes about the design. 

First, the interaction stinks. The most that goes on between players is that you hope that they don't take the card that you want.  

Second, this game really suffers from an exponential growth problem, if you aren't in contention for the lead at the beginning of the game you won't be at the end.  

Lastly, where are the tough choices? Most of the cards are best or second best. It feels more like an exercise than a game.  So, often it feels like you are making false decisions throughout.

Overall, I liken it to having sex with a corpse, it gets the job done, but it leaves you a bit cold.

Update: Played this yet again to give it yet another chance both live and on BSW, I decided that perhaps I should downgrade my rating.  Then I realized I was right with my initial rating.  So it remains a solid and strong 3.

Update: Hey, it's been seven years since I've played this last. I thought that I should update my rating, but it turns out that, yet again, I had the same emotional response from it as before.  Frustrating and unfulfilled.  I won and I felt like I didn't make any relevant decisions to my position, rather I just got the right cards at the right time, more than other people did.  Turn order really makes all the worst parts of this game downright stupid.

RATING: 7.5
Really a good game, but in my opinion, has some drawbacks that bring the rating down a bit. Firstly, like some other older games, it suffers from a runaway leader problem. In other words, if you make a mistake in the beginning that allows another player to get ahead, it's likely they will stay ahead and you will know shortly that you do not have any chance of winning at all. Also, relative to other euros, (such as Macao, for example) this game has a limited amount of viable options to partake in. I feel sort of forced to do certain things at certain times, which limits any feeling of control. There can be times during this game when really bad things happen to you, and it is based on luck, and there is absolutely nothing you can do about it - again, a loss of control. Other than these things, the game flows well and is quite fast, which is nice. It can feel dry and programmed though - although I must say that I have never played with the expansions - i hear they take away some of the problems inherent in the original.

RATING: 3
Saint Petersburg isn't terrible. The core mechanic is elegant enough. The problem is, after one play the best strategy is obvious. The shape of that strategy depends on the card draw and not much else. Player choices aren't difficult once each understands how the game works. As a result, I see it playing out the same way again and again. You can block other players, but because money is so tight, the opportunity cost is high; incentives favour those who free ride on the blocking player's efforts. Fun or interesting moves are rarely optimal. It's a cold, lifeless exercise.

RATING: 10
It really is basically a card game, with the board being superfluous, although it does look nice.  Definitely a fun card game, though, with easy to learn rules, depth, and some interesting decisions.  Should appeal to many casual and serious gamers, but perhaps not to the extremes in either group. I'm pretty sure that the noble cards are the key to victory.  Not only can you rack up a good score with them at the end of the game, but they also provide you with funds during the game, as well as a handful of victory points.  Having at least one extra helps too, so you can purchase an upgrade during the exchange phase without losing a unique card.  It's good to buy some craftsmen, especially early on, and the buildings may be overrated, although you need to have a feel for when to buy them so you don't end up with excess cash, since St. Pete is a game of extreme efficiency.  Update:  overtook Ticket To Ride as my favorite game of 2004.  Has the potential to become a classic that will be played for years to come.  Might be my favorite game since Ra.  Excellent for two, three, or four players.  How many games fit that criteria?  I'm addicted.  Further update:  THE BEST GAME EVER!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I played this game just in time to keep an eye out for the second edition because I really liked it.

This is a somewhat economic tableau building game.  First, it has a really clever player order mechanic that I really enjoy.  Each round consists of 4 phases and each player in a 4 player game gets one token that represents a phase they go first in (and play continues clockwise from there during that phase).  These are passed each round so there is a neat little structure of turn order that jumps around during any individual round.

Each phase a different kind of card is drawn from a deck to fill a market track.  Players in turn order for that phase will buy these cards adding them to their tableau or take them into their hand which is limited to 3 cards.  The first phase cards will provide mostly money income, the second phase mostly points, the third phase is mostly money again but also provide large end-of-game point bonuses based on set collection.  The final phase is upgrade cards to increase the effectiveness of the cards built in the other 3 phases.

This is such a succinct and clever game, I found myself really enjoying it and there is a ton of strategy to mine out of the simple gameplay.  It's also not too hard to teach and plays at a pretty decent clip.  It is not great with 3 players though as one player each round will have 2 of the 4 phase tokens.  It is great with 4 and I've heard works well with 2 as well where each player will have 2 tokens.

Only negative thing I can say about this is "ugh, paper money".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
St. Petersburg is an interesting card game where you buy cards from a row of up to 8 cards in player order.  There are four types of cards, workers produce money, buildings produce VP’s, aristocrats produce money (but less than workers) but provide end game VP’s, and the fourth type is trading cards which are basically special upgrades for each of the other three types.  The game is played in phases, first the worker phase where workers are added to the board, then scored, and then it moves to building phase where buildings are purchased and scored, etc... In any case, it seems like a fine game but just another example of building your money train early and knowing when to switch gears to buying lots of VP generating cards.  It is worth more play before I commit to really liking it or not.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
I can see why a lot of people like this game.  It has all the elements of a good Euro.  The problem I have with the game is the lack of player interaction combined with a lack of really engaging gameplay.  Basically you just go off and do your own thing and try to do it better than your opponent.  Of course this alone isn't such a bad thing, but if I'm going to play a game that lacks player interaction my solitaire experience needs to be very rewarding for me to like the game.  In the case of St. Petersburg, the solitaire experience was just okay, hence my middling rating of the game.  Part of the problem may have been that I played a 2-player game, but maybe not because others claim this is the optimal number of players resulting in the most "pure" experience the game has to offer.  If this is true, then I know for sure my rating will stay where it is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Set-collecting card game with a city building theme. The game consists of several rounds comprising of four turns. On each turn a number of cards (up to eight) are revealed from four decks (workers, buildings, aristocrats, and upgrades to previously acquired cards from the three other decks). Players take it in turns to purchase the buildings and add them to their tableau, and these in turn provide benefits throughout the remainder of the game e.g. workers produce money to purchase more cards, buildings award victory points, and aristocrats a combination of the two. Points are also awarded at the end of the game for having a variety of different aristocrats in the player's city. 'Saint Petersburg' is a pleasingly simple and streamlined game to play in comparison to other similar set-collection and efficiently obtaining victory points games, but it maintains a strategic depth to the gameplay and this ensures that it deserves to be played repeatedly by fans of this style of game.

RATING: 7
There`re 4 types phases in each round. In the first you can hire workesr - they will give you money. In the second you can buy buildings - they give mainly points. In the third you can get aristocrates. They give some money, sometimes points. They are more expensive than workers and buildings, but gives you many bonus points at the end of the game. Usually you can`t wi without a majority in the aristocrats. That`s no good. The building stategy is not so strong. The New Society expansion changes it. In the forth phase you can get upgrade cards (for all 3 types of cards).

You don1t have maoney to get every card, that you want, but you can take up to 3 cards on your hand and pay for them later. When you have a card, you pay 1 less if you buy the same card again. You buy also 1 less if the card is from the previous round.

You must see how many cards will come in the next phase (when you will be forth and there will be only 3 cards, maybe its good to buy a card, then there will be 4 cards, specially when this are aristocrates.

I like the game, but don1t like that the aristocrates are so strong.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.1
Our initial plays of this fine game left me feeling absolutely clueless. In fact I despaired so much I logged on to the strategy section  of the game page here on BGG.

Once I had absorbed some of the lessons to be learned I proceeded to kick my dear wife from here and to Aarhus. A pattern was established in which I would continue to do so, though she slow but steadily was catching on to me.

The game itself is very dry. You buy workers who earn you cash. Buildings who earn cash and/ or victory points or sometimes special abilities. Advisors who again earn cash and/ or victory points and finally special cards that are upgrades of workers/ buildings/ advisors.

You rinse and repeat. The game scores or pay out after each specific phase (ie workers/ buildings/ advisors). It is a balancing act of getting the right workers plus cash so you can still get the right buildings and advisors, not to mention the special buildings later on.

Overspending in the worker phase may mean you miss out on some cool buildings or in particular advisors in later phases.

The neat trick is to get the advisors that will get you points and cash. The earlier in the game you get them, the sooner they will earn themselves and start providing a surplus.

Game end follows when one of the stacks (workers etc.) are depleted. There are more specifics such as card rows, cards being moved down and becoming cheaper etc. but you get the gist...

Returning to the initial comments, then we come to a state where I feel I have done all there is and where there are no challenges to be had. It may be group-think (I only play against my wife), it may be that different players mean different strategies or making it harder to execute said strategies.

I like the game, I can see past the drab colours and see there is a good game here - which is also reflected in the score - even if we have sold the game.

RATING: 5.5
A deep game that also manages to be very simple at the same time.  I enjoy multiple paths to victory games, and there are all kinds of ways to go about winning St. Pete.  I can see that, although the appearance of cards changes every time, the game could get a little programmed.  At its essence, it is a worker placement/economic engine game--place your resources here, get this in return, all the while building your cache--that manages to toss money management to the wind (money is only tight if you plan poorly, otherwise it is easy to come by).  

2 PLAYER:  The biggest problem with Saint Pete 2P is that a player can be completely controlled by how the cards come out.  The game really tricks you into thinking it is high strategy, but, in the end, and after several plays, it becomes apparent that the player with the best strategy does not always win--the player who gets the best cards falling to him does.  The players have less control over the game than the game has over them.  I have a hard time with games that masquerade as something they are not.  This is reflected in my rating.

RATING: 4
TRADED AWAY (2/2/08) --- This game has steadily dropped in rating for me.  It started at 9 after the first playing, but after a couple more plays dropped to an 8.  After staying at an 8 for a while, it has since dropped to a 6.  I guess this is because every game of St. Petersburg is very similar to every other game of St. Petersburg.  Buy lots of workers, buy a few buildings, buy as many different aristocrats as possible.  Some of the cards are unique and interesting, but most are almost identical with only slight differences.  I think this is a well designed game, that is great fun the first few times you play it.  But it simply doesn't stand up to numerous repeated plays.

RATING: 7
[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/9217/saint-petersburg]Saint Petersburg[/url] was a game I played, so far, only on Yucata, so all of the meta-game that happens around the table is lost.

As is, the game has many interesting decisions to be made throughout. I'm still not 100% sure of how the phases of the game works, but Yucata deals with this matter for me. What I do know is that the flow of the game is well made and makes sense: with the works you get money, to pay for buildings and to sustain the nobles and the get people to do more refine work.

Every type of cards (workers, buildings and nobles) has its own phase, when you collect money and VPs for the next phase - this is something I liked quite a bit.

I can't say much about the time of a game (going by Yucata I will say: around ten days!). I can say that the game scales well, but has no catch-up mechanics, so once someone has a good money-VPs machine working, say goodbye.

The price for [b]Saint Petersburg[/b] is somewhat high, and has a on-off relation with my wishlist. So far, it will stay off, but I do want to play some more of it, so I hope I can convince someone in my game group to buy it! Will see.

RATING: 7.5
2.48
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Saint Petersburg is an innovative and fun game that marries strategic economic management with careful planning. At its heart is the buying of workers that make money, that allow to buy buildings, which earn victory points, aristocrats, which do a little of both and also score bonus points at the end of the game for the more you have, and trading cards that allow to upgrade existing cards. I have read some criticism on the balance of power of some cards from the base game, which I understand leads to some unforgiving experience if you make poor decision early on. Therefore my one tip for this game is never spunk all your money at the end of each round so you have money to buy workers with in the following round! However, on the flip side, don't get left behind on VP in the building round. Love the scenario and artwork. Certainly one of our favourites in the collection.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Gain fame by building 18th century Saint Petersburg - players develop an economy by acquiring workers, buildings, and attracting aristocrats with the goal of scoring the most "fame" points. Takes a game or two to get a handle on the strategy and how the cards interact but the game is no harder than "gateway" in difficulty level, though I think it's best suited as a "next step" game. There are been criticisms about the art but I quite like the thematic Russian graphics. Components and cards are excellent quality. Solid game that shows its depths through repeated plays. Works well but has a different flavor at 2, 3, or 4 players (I suggest taking out the Pubs at 2P though, because there's a lot of money to go around and they break the game, especially if one player can horde them all).

RATING: 5
A 4th play showed even less redeeming quality than I expected - really the only neat thing about this game is the distinct phases and how new cards come out during them; nothing more.  It seems like it should be best with 3, but the way the phases work for 3 players is awkward.

The first phase feels fairly pointless, as it is essentially a random draw for who gets a better deal on income generation.  The second phase is then flush with buildings that nobody wants because they are underpowered, but people may grab some simply so they have the option of getting an aristocrat.  

Aristocrats are clearly stronger in general than buildings, considering their benefit during the game is fairly comparable yet they score insanely at the end.  The end of the game also feels very silly, where you have a final chance to buy upgrades, and if there are no aristocrats there is no reason to buy anything.  The Observatory is, in general, extremely strong as well.

So overall, the game has clear balance issues, and almost nothing clever enough to make up for its significant flaws.

RATING: N/A
Saint Petersburg is a card game in which you acquire workers for income, build buildings for fame, and attract aristocrats to your city in order to gain the most fame at the end of the game.

Card game deals with 'gracious living along the river Neva': the baroque palaces, wide boulevards, and imposing bridges of St. Petersburg. On May 16th, 1703, Czar Peter laid the cornerstone for the first building. Quickly, glorious buildings were added, always being expanded, so that Nobility (as well as victory-bringing Fame Points) may want to move in. But to accomplish this, one needs merchants who can bankroll the necessary Rubles, or the glory is over. The competition isn't sleeping either, and can sometimes steal a desired card right out from under your nose.

Online Play

BrettspielWelt (real-time)
Yucata (turn-based)
A standalone PC version can be downloaded from Westpark Gamers.

Expanded by:
Saint Petersburg - The Banquet
Saint Petersburg Expansion

RATING: 8
This is probably the one "engine" game that gamers could use to introduce the concept to folks just getting into the hobby.  It's fairly straightforward, and new players can have a reasonably good first experience with the game, so long as the experienced players offer up suggestions and tips during the course of the game.  That I've played it so many times, and still want to play it again, speaks volumes to how well the game holds up.

1 play: 2 players

RATING: 7.3
This game is showing it's age but is still a classic!  I enjoy the art style and card play a lot.  Deciding if you want to go for cards that give you income or points is always a tough decision.  As a long term planner, I usually go for generating money but this is one of those game where you can go for a powerful point scoring card in the beginning of the game and still win against a money generating player.  The set collection aspect is wonderfully implemented and adds another layer of depth to this great, classic design.  There is a lot of strategy to be found and this makes an excellent spouse game.

Note:  Sleeved with Premium Mayday Mini Euro Sleeves

RATING: 6.9
I thought this was really a interesting and tactical game. Never seen it in a store before, until a couple of weeks ago. Could pick it up for half the price, and so we did. Started to set-up the game and read the rules. Easy game to explain, and within 15 minutes we were playing. Didn’t know what was wise to do at the beginning. Money is scarce in the beginning of the game, and you should find a way to generate income. But also points are welcome. And the aristocrats will generate small income and/or some points, but they can give lots of points at the final counting of points. Decisions, decisions, decisions. But….

After playing two or three rounds, it becomes clear what would be wise to do. The game becomes a bit of automatic playing. There are no more surprises. It’s a nice game for every now and they, but the re-playability-factor of this game isn’t too high.

RATING: 9
I can't get enough of this game.  The careful management of your funds; the ability to completely shoot yourself in the foot, but only have to suffer for the short duration of the game before trying again, because you usually know what you did wrong.  Yet it's so easy to be tempted to err again.  This game is brilliant!  For the longest time, I'd only played it on BrettSpielWelt, and feared that keeping track of everyone's income and all that could be an accounting nightmare which could really detract from the fun.  In reality, the biggest thing missing is the cool snippets of Russian music to prompt the players.  :^)

RATING: 8
After 5+ Plays: Quickly becoming one of my favorites.  

After 10+ Plays: An economic engine game that is boiled down to its very essence, and teeters on the edge of being too simple.  I like it a lot though and am pleasantly surprised, in light of its simplicity, that it has held up after repeated plays.

After 15+ Plays: Lowering rating from 9 to 8.  Considering how little strategic variety there is, I'm surprised how many plays this game kept my interest for.  Certainly still enjoyable for an occasional play, but it's past its prime.

RATING: 8
Карточная игра, в которой мы покупаем свои активы с "рынка карт". До предела оголённая механика, присутствующая в некоторых других играх. Отлично сбалансирована, не так просто просчитывается.

Минусы - фан есть лишь в соревновании. Через несколько игр понимаешь, что при малом числе игроков рулят синие карты и деньги, а при большом - дворяне. Зачастую выбор карты для покупки определяется тем, что есть, хотя эффект трёх "И" ("игра играет игроком") закамуфлирован.

RATING: N/A
A fun card-based victory point and money engine building game by using deck building and card drafting mechanics. On each round you can purchase workers to make more money, use the money that's produced to buy buildings and aristocrats (each worth victory points and/or money), and if you have any left over, buy upgrades. Rinse, repeat. I'm not really too wild about the starting player cards (they simply serve no other purpose), cumbersome scoring track (it takes a couple of plays to figure them out), and player pieces (they don't seem to fit on the scoring track itself), player pieces (why do you need two of each color?). There are possible runaway leader problems if you don't snag a couple of critical cards. The downside is that the path to victory always appears to be the same, based on catch-up really; indebt yourself reserving expensive cards, then sling-shot back to the top after paying for them.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
